                  </table>
            </div>
            
            
            <div class="article-section__table-source"></div>
         </div>
         
         <p>To further confirm the presence of carbon, Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0002">2</a> shows the Raman spectra of NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01, and NBTP-0.02. It can be observed that there are three obvious Raman characteristic peaks for all the above samples. The peak at 1354 cm<sup>−1</sup> (D band) and the peak at 1600 cm<sup>−1</sup>(G band) correspond to the amorphous carbon and the graphitic carbon, respectively. Moreover, the peak at 1001 cm<sup>−1</sup> represents the stretching vibration of P−O bonds in phosphate tetrahedra, and the characteristic peak of PO<sub>4</sub><sup>3−</sup> is rather weak.<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0029_R_d261297400e1101" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - J. Appl. Electrochem.">29</a></sup></span> Furthermore, the intensity ratio of D band and G band (<i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub>) can be estimated to evaluate the degree of defection in carbon for the above samples. Thus, the values of <i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub> of NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01, and NBTP-0.02 can be calculated to be 1.18, 1.11, 1.10, and 1.11, respectively, suggesting the amorphous nature of the carbon coatings in the above-mentioned four samples, which is consistent with the above-mentioned XRD results.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="batt202400767-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/773e08d8-f470-4700-a365-f2107149c9c4/batt202400767-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/773e08d8-f470-4700-a365-f2107149c9c4/batt202400767-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/91c5a845-39dc-4bb3-af77-2eb0c267dd72/batt202400767-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/773e08d8-f470-4700-a365-f2107149c9c4/batt202400767-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=batt202400767-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fbatt.202400767" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Raman spectra of NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01, and NBTP-0.02.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0003">3</a> illustrates SEM images of NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01, and NBTP-0.02. In comparison with the NTP, the other three Bi-doped samples show the stronger agglomeration in the secondary microscale particles, possibly due to the formation of the smaller primary nanoparticles of NTP resulted from the Bi doping. Moreover, all the samples are composed of primary nanoparticles about 200–400 nm as presented in the inset of Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0003">3c</a>. As can be seen, the morphology of the four samples is composed of scattered irregular particles with sizes ranging from hundreds of nanometers to several microns. Thus, there is no significant difference in the particle morphology between the NTP and Bi-doped samples, suggesting that Bi doping has little effect on the morphology of NTP. In addition, the EDS elemental mapping of NBTP-0.01 is also displayed in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0003">3</a>, indicating that Na, Bi, Ti and P elements are uniformly distributed in the sample. It can be also confirmed that the Bi element is successfully introduced into the NTP material.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="batt202400767-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e416af9c-7a7b-4307-b2f8-faf7e65e0872/batt202400767-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/e416af9c-7a7b-4307-b2f8-faf7e65e0872/batt202400767-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/0ff9f53a-df1c-4f80-915b-44ecf8836869/batt202400767-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e416af9c-7a7b-4307-b2f8-faf7e65e0872/batt202400767-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=batt202400767-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fbatt.202400767" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>SEM images of NTP (a), NBTP-0.005 (b), NBTP-0.01 (c), and NBTP-0.02 (d), with the EDS elemental mapping of NBTP-0.01 included.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>To further characterize the particle morphologies, Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0004">4</a> gives TEM images of NTP and NBTP-0.01. The carbon layer with the thickness of about 5 nm can be observed to be compactly coated at the NTP particle for both the NTP and NBTP-0.01 samples, predominately owing to the high-temperature decomposition of citric acid in the precursors to ensure good electronic conductivity of the samples. Clear lattice stripes can be seen in Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0004">4b</a> and <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0004">d</a>, with interplanar spacing of 0.159 and 0.180 nm, corresponding to the (116) and (110) crystal plane of NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, respectively. It is also indicated that both the as-synthesized NTP and NBTP-0.01 show good crystallinity.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="batt202400767-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/c1b56911-a0c9-4294-a62b-88abf3fd3fa6/batt202400767-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/c1b56911-a0c9-4294-a62b-88abf3fd3fa6/batt202400767-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/9bae6d4f-801d-4de5-97ad-932513beeb57/batt202400767-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/c1b56911-a0c9-4294-a62b-88abf3fd3fa6/batt202400767-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=batt202400767-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fbatt.202400767" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>TEM images of NTP (a, b) and NBTP-0.01(c, d), (e) Full XPS spectrum of NBTP-0.01, (f) Bi 4 f high-resolution XPS spectrum of NBTP-0.01, (g) Ti 2p high-resolution XPS spectrum of NBTP-0.01.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) was conducted with the carbon (C 1s=284 eV) applied to calibrate binding energies, in an attempt to confirm the elemental composition and valence state in NBTP-0.01, as shown in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0004">4</a>. Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0004">4e</a> gives the XPS full spectrum of the NBTP-0.01, suggesting that the binding energies at 1073, 532, 460, 284, 163 and 133 eV correspond to Na 1s, O 1s, Ti 2p, C 1s, Bi 4 f, and P 2p, respectively.<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0029_R_d261297400e1224" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - J. Appl. Electrochem.">29</a></sup></span> It should be noted that the Bi 4 f peak is rather low in the full spectra of Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0004">4e</a>, also indicating a low amount of Bi element introduced into the NTP lattice. Then, the high-resolution spectrum of Bi 4 f was further detected, as shown in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0004">4f</a>. It can be observed from Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0004">4f</a> that two distinct peaks are located at 164.9 and 159.6 eV corresponding to Bi<sup>3+</sup> 4f<sub>5/2</sub> and Bi<sup>3+</sup> 4f<sub>7/2</sub>,<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0046_R_d261297400e1245" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">46</a></sup></span> indicating that Bi<sup>3+</sup> is successfully introduced into the NTP lattice. Moreover, to have a better understanding of the variety of the valence states of Ti, Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0004">4g</a> shows the high-resolution spectrum of Ti 2p in the same sample. It shows that there are two diffraction peaks for the NBTP-0.01 sample at around 460.0 (Peak 1) and 465.8 eV (Peak 2) with respect to Ti<sup>4+</sup> 2p<sub>3/2</sub> and Ti<sup>4+</sup> 2p<sub>1/2</sub>,<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0029_R_d261297400e1263" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - J. Appl. Electrochem.">29</a></sup></span> which are well consistent with the Ti<sup>4+</sup> ions in an octahedral environment of NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>.</p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">As shown in Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0005">5</a>–<a href="#batt202400767-fig-0008">8</a>, all the electrochemical and charge/discharge curves of the corresponding NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01 and NBTP-0.02 samples were examined with a conventional three-electrode cell using a platinum foil as the counter electrode and a saturated calomel electrode (SCE, 0.244 V) as the reference electrode. In order to investigate the electrochemical behavior among the NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01, and NBTP-0.02 anode materials, cyclic voltammetry (CV) was conducted to examine the electrochemical reaction activities at these four electrodes in 1.0 M Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> aqueous solution at a scan rate of 0.5 mV s<sup>−1</sup>. As shown in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0005">5a</a>, there are a pair of redox peaks for all the above samples at around −0.9 and −0.78 V, with respect to the Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox reaction in Na<sub>1+x</sub>Bi<sub>x</sub>Ti<sub>2-x</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, accompanying with the intercalation/extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> in the NTP lattice. The corresponding electrochemical reaction is as follows:
            <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202400767-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/3075ff44-7ad3-448b-937d-e7024d453dc9/batt202400767-math-0001.png"></span><math></math>
                  </span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>
            </div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="batt202400767-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/353c542a-8c95-4cee-9f56-bf078d4d0a3e/batt202400767-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/353c542a-8c95-4cee-9f56-bf078d4d0a3e/batt202400767-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/19cec97c-8c0c-472b-a25e-1625da998377/batt202400767-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/353c542a-8c95-4cee-9f56-bf078d4d0a3e/batt202400767-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=batt202400767-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fbatt.202400767" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Electrochemical performance of NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01, and NBTP-0.02: (a) cyclic voltammetry curve; (b) charge discharge curve at 2 C; (c) rate performance; (d) cyclic performance at 1 C.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>For the NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01 and NBTP-0.02 samples, the doped Bi<sup>3+</sup> has the electrochemical inertness and does not participate in the electrochemical reactions. Bi doped-NTP, especially NBTP-0.01, has the higher peak current density in contrast with NTP. Moreover, the peak current density of NBTP-0.005 and NBTP-0.02 are also smaller than that of NBTP-0.01. The values of the separations between the oxidation and the reduction peak potentials (Δ<i>E</i><sub>p</sub>) for the NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01 and NBTP-0.02 anodes are estimated to be 126, 128, 124 and 140 mV, respectively. It suggests that the NBTP-0.01 anode has the highest reaction current, the smallest value of Δ<i>E</i><sub>p</sub>, and thus the best reaction activity among the four ones, also suggesting that NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> doped with an appropriate amount of bismuth has the better electrode reaction activity with respect to the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation/extraction compared to the pristine sample. The better electrochemical kinetics resulted from the Bi doping is probably due to the larger transport channel for Na<sup>+</sup> ions in the Bi-modified NTP crystal structure in this work. However, it should be noted that the NBTP-0.01 has the best electrode activity, rather than the NBTP-0.02 with the more added Bi (x=0.02), might owing to the decrease in the theoretical capacity of Na<sub>1+x</sub>Bi<sub>x</sub>Ti<sub>2-x</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> active materials with increasing the inactive bismuth.</p>
         
         <p>Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0005">5b</a> shows the charge/discharge curves of the NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01 and NBTP-0.02 samples at a 2 C-rate, All the samples show a charge/discharge voltage plateau around −0.83 V (vs. SCE) with respect to the Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox reaction in Na<sub>1+x</sub>Bi<sub>x</sub>Ti<sub>2−x</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, which is consistent with the CV results in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0005">5a</a>. It can be observed that the discharge capacity of the undoped NTP sample is 79.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>. As the amount of the bismuth doping increases from 0 to 0.01, its discharge capacity gradually increases, with the value of 104.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> for the NBTP-0.01 sample. However, further increasing the doping amount to be x=0.02, the discharge capacity of the NBTP-0.02 one decreases to be 94.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>. This may be due to that the substitution of Ti with excessive electrochemically inert bismuth leads to a decrease in the theoretical capacity of the anode, which is consistent with the CV results in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0005">5a</a>. Of course, the largest capacity value of 104.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> for the NBTP-0.01 sample, more than that of 79.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>for the pristine one, also might be resulted from the larger transport channel for Na<sup>+</sup> ions with the Bi doping in this work.</p>
         
         <p>Further tests were conducted on the rate and cycling performance of the above-mentioned four samples. Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0005">5c</a> presents the plots of the discharge capacities vs. cycle number for the NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01, and NBTP-0.02 at varying rates including 2, 5, 10, 20 C-rate, and back to 2 C-rate. NBTP-0.01 provides the discharge capacities of 104.8, 94.4, 88.6 and 81.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 2, 5, 10 and 20 C rates, respectively, and retains a discharge capacity of 104.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a high capacity retention of 99.3 % when returning to 2 C-rate. The corresponding smaller values for the NTP sample are 79.6 (2 C), 66.3 (5 C), 59.7 (10 C), and 51.1 (20 C) and retains 76.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention of 96.1 %, in comparison with the NBTP-0.01 sample. Therefore, it can be also observed from the plots of Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0005">5c</a> that the NBTP-0.01 has the best rate performance with the largest discharge capacity and the highest capacity retention at different C-rates among the four samples. Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0005">5d</a> shows the plots of discharge capacity as a function of cycle number for the NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01, and NBTP-0.02 samples at 1 C rate for 50 cycles. All samples show a certain degree of capacity decay during the cycling of the charge/discharge process, which may be caused by some side reactions at the electrode/electrolyte interface. The initial discharge capacity of NBTP-0.01 is 130.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, and after 50 cycles, the capacity is 109.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention of 84.5 %. In contrast, NTP has an initial discharge capacity of 106.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, and after 50 cycles, the capacity is 71.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention rate of 67.5 %. It is indicated that the NBTP-0.01 has the better cycling performance than that of the NTP. Thereby, the NBTP-0.01 has the best rate performance with the largest discharge capacity and the best cycling performance among the above-mentioned four samples. The above-mentioned previous work<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0046_R_d261297400e1523" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">46</a></sup></span> on the introduction of Bi into NVP to form Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2-x</sub>Bi<sub>x</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C, also reported that the introduction of bismuth ions slightly increases the cell size, while the solid BiO<sub>6</sub> serve as a stable and larger diffusion channel for the migration of Na<sup>+</sup> within the NVP structure, thus exhibiting a longer cycle life and higher rate performance for the modified composites in comparison with the pristine one. Consequently, the best rate performance and cycling performance for the modified NBTP-0.01 composite also might be due to the possible formed solid BiO<sub>6</sub> octahedra served as a stable and larger diffusion channel for the migration of Na<sup>+</sup> within the NTP structure in this work.</p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">Furthermore, the reaction kinetics of NTP and NBTP-0.01 at various scanning rates were examined using the CV method, as seen in Figures. <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0006">6a</a> and <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0006">b</a>. As shown in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0006">6c</a>, the plots of <i>I</i><sub>p</sub> vs. <i>ν</i><sup>1/2</sup> can be obtained from the CV curves of Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0006">6a</a> and <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0006">b</a>. It illustrates that there is a linear relationship between the peak current (<i>I</i><sub>p</sub>) and the square root of the scan rate (<i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>), indicating that the electrochemical reactions for the NTP and NBTP-0.01 samples are the typical diffusion-controlled processes. The Randles- Sevcik equation can be shown as follows:<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0029_R_d261297400e1578" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - J. Appl. Electrochem.">29</a></sup></span><div class="inline-equation" id="batt202400767-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/c70a17fe-91a4-4b77-98cc-3698a65f2e68/batt202400767-math-0002.png"></span><math></math>
                  </span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>
            </div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="batt202400767-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/6b77bc9a-07ac-4401-a674-4aed01a69a9f/batt202400767-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/6b77bc9a-07ac-4401-a674-4aed01a69a9f/batt202400767-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1b1cfa37-a7a0-4786-8e44-6314054f5f0c/batt202400767-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/6b77bc9a-07ac-4401-a674-4aed01a69a9f/batt202400767-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=batt202400767-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fbatt.202400767" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Cyclic voltammograms of NTP (a) and NBTP-0.01 (b) at various scan rates, and the relationship between peak current (<i>I</i>p) and the square root of scan rate (<i>v</i>1/2).</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>In the equation, <i>I</i><sub>p</sub> is the peak current of the cathode or anode, <i>n</i> is the number of electrons per molecule during embedding, F is Faraday constant, R is gas constant, <i>T</i> is absolute temperature, <i>A</i> is the effective contact area between the electrode and electrolyte, <i>C</i> is the concentration of Na<sup>+</sup> in the electrode, <i>D</i> is the diffusion coefficient of Na<sup>+</sup>, and <i>v</i> is the scan rate. According to Equation (2), the diffusion coefficients of the anode and cathode processes of NTP can be calculated to be 1.65×10<sup>−8</sup> and 1.37×10<sup>−8</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The corresponding diffusion coefficients of NBTP-0.01 are 6.72×10<sup>−8</sup> and 6.58×10<sup>−8</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. It suggests that the diffusion coefficients of Na<sup>+</sup> for the NBTP-0.01 anode are higher than those for the NTP anode. It is also confirmed that the larger transport channel for Na<sup>+</sup> ions in the crystal structure by the Bi doping can evidently accelerate the ion diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> and improve the intrinsic ion conductivity of the Bi-modified system, thus promoting the electrochemical kinetics and the charge/discharge capacities.</p>
         
         <p>Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0007">7</a> shows the long-term cycling performance of the NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01, and NBTP-0.02 half-cells at a 10 C-rate. The NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01and NBTP-0.02 half-cells deliver the initial discharge capacities of 61.4, 72.0, 87.7 and 70.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 200 cycles, with the corresponding capacity retention of 77.5 %, 78.5 %, 79.2 % and 75.5 %, respectively. Thereby, it can be obtained that the NBTP-0.01 half-cell has the highest capacity retention and thus the best cycling performance among the four samples. It further suggests that the appropriate amount of Bi doping is greatly beneficial to enhance the long-term cycling performance of the above-mentioned system, also owing to that the possible formed solid BiO<sub>6</sub> octahedra serves as a stable and larger diffusion channel for the migration of Na<sup>+</sup> within the NTP structure by the Bi doping.<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0046_R_d261297400e1733" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">46</a></sup></span>
            </p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="batt202400767-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/0322d7af-0809-4581-bd9d-caec6678552f/batt202400767-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/0322d7af-0809-4581-bd9d-caec6678552f/batt202400767-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/ddcce837-d77b-412d-a1a1-3010dcf8de08/batt202400767-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/0322d7af-0809-4581-bd9d-caec6678552f/batt202400767-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=batt202400767-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fbatt.202400767" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Cycle performance of NTP, NBTP-0.005, NBTP-0.01, and NBTP-0.02 at 10 C</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>The hydrogen evolution phenomenon that easily occurs at the anode potential is a huge obstacle for the application of anode materials in ASIBs. Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0008">8a</a> gives the linear voltammetry (LSV) curves of the NTP and NBTP-0.01 anodes in 1.0 M Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> aqueous solution at 1.0 mV s<sup>−1</sup>. It can be clearly observed from the plots of Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0008">8a</a> that the bismuth doping can shift the hydrogen evolution potential negatively and thus suppress the hydrogen evolution at the anode. In order to confirm the effect of the bismuth doping on the hydrogen evolution potential at the NTP anode, Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0008">8b</a> and <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0008">c</a> present the charge/discharge plots of the above-mentioned NTP and NBTP-0.01 half-cells with different discharge cut-off voltages. It is obvious that the possibility of the occurrence of hydrogen evolution at a discharge voltage can be estimated by the slope of the tangent lines at the end of the discharge curves in Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0008">8b</a> and <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0008">c</a>.<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0042_R_d261297400e1786" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - J. Mater. Chem. A">42</a></sup></span> When the discharge cut-off voltages for the corresponding half-cells are set at −1.1 V (vs. SCE), there are similar tangent slopes for the discharge plots of the NTP and NBTP-0.01 half-cells, suggesting the little possibility of the occurrence of hydrogen evolution on this condition. Then, when the discharge cut-off voltage is set at −1.2 V (vs. SCE), it can be observed that a new voltage plateau with respect to the possible hydrogen evolution reaction occurs at the end of the discharge curve of the NTP half-cell in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0008">8c</a>, however, not observed for the NBTP-0.01 one. It reflects that the hydrogen evolution reaction at the NTP anode is easier to occur than that at the NBTP-0.01 anode, further confirming that the bismuth doping can help suppress the hydrogen evolution reaction at the anode, thereby broadening the discharge cut-off voltage and enhancing the battery capacity.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="batt202400767-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e9371732-eeec-47b1-98b0-f05cf2e0124c/batt202400767-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/e9371732-eeec-47b1-98b0-f05cf2e0124c/batt202400767-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/ca911b94-4e89-4c46-a425-843db6460436/batt202400767-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e9371732-eeec-47b1-98b0-f05cf2e0124c/batt202400767-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=batt202400767-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fbatt.202400767" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>(a) LSV curves of NTP and NBTP-0.01; (b) charge/discharge curves with the cut-off voltage of −1.1 V; (c) charge/discharge curves with the cut-off voltage of −1.2 V.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>In the specific case of the hydrogen reaction mechanism, a two-step scheme has been confirmed:<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0047_R_d261297400e1818" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Electrochim. Acta">47</a>, <a href="#batt202400767-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0048_R_d261297400e1818" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - J. Electroanal. Chem.">48</a></sup></span> a first step consisting in the discharge of the hydrated proton (H<sup>+</sup> electronation) and a following second step that could be either a recombination of the adsorbed hydrogen atoms (chemical desorption) or an ion-atom recombination known as electrochemical desorption. Either one of these steps can be rate determining, which results in the possibility of four distinct mechanisms for the hydrogen reaction. Furthermore, it has been reported that metals having more unpaired electrons in the d-band have a lower percentage of d-character, or more “holes” in the d-band, and because of the vacant orbitals in the d-band, these metals interact strongly with electron donating atoms or molecules, and hence adsorb hydrogen strongly by electron pair formation.<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0049_R_d261297400e1823" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Electrochim. Acta">49</a></sup></span> Since the Bi element has 6 unpaired electrons in the d-band, more than 2 for the Ti element, it can be indicated that the Bi element might adsorb hydrogen more strongly by electron pair formation in contrast with the Ti element. Thus, it can be considered that the incorporation of Bi into NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> might result in the stronger adsorption (the more difficult electrochemical desorption) of the H atom on the anode surface, further suggesting the higher hydrogen evolution overpotentials at the Bi-modified NTP/C anode in this work. In fact, N. PAPAGEORGIO et al<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0047_R_d261297400e1833" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Electrochim. Acta">47</a></sup></span> also investigated the effect of Bi content on the kinetics of the hydrogen evolution reaction at various Bi-containing Pb binary alloy electrodes, and proposed that the dominant mechanism for the hydrogen evolution reaction on Pb is changing with increasing Bi content from a rate-determining discharge followed by electrochemical desorption, to a fast discharge followed by a rate-determining electrochemical desorption in the case of the pure Bi electrode, probably due to the stronger hydrogen adsorption on the electrode surface resulted from the addition of the Bi element. Therefore, it is further confirmed that the introduction of Bi can inhibit the occurrence of the hydrogen evolution reaction at the modified anode in this work.</p>
         
         <p>Based on the above results, an anode-limited full cell system of NTP//NMO (or NBTP-0.01//NMO) was further assembled by using Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> as the cathode material and 1.0 M Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> aqueous solution as the electrolyte. Due to its large “S” – shaped tunnel with an internal open framework structure, NMO promotes a rapid intercalation/extraction of Na<sup>+</sup>, making it a promising candidate material for the ASIB cathode.<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0050_R_d261297400e1850" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Energy Technol.">50</a>-<a href="#batt202400767-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0052_R_d261297400e1850" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Electrochem. Commun.">52</a></sup></span> In order to achieve anode-limited capacity balance, the mass ratio of the cathode and anode active materials can be reasonably set to be about 2.4 : 1.0 based on their theoretical capacities, resulting in a capacity ratio of approximately 1.2 : 1.0.</p>
         
         <p>In order to investigate the electrochemical reaction kinetics of the above-mentioned NTP and NBTP-0.01 anodes in full cells, Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9a</a> illustrates the CV curves of the corresponding aqueous full cells at 0.5 mVs<sup>−1</sup>. As shown in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9a</a>, both the CV curves of the two full-cells show three oxidation peaks and two reduction peaks companying with the similar intercalation/extraction processes of Na<sup>+</sup>. Compared with the NTP//NMO full-cell, the NBTP-0.01//NMO full-cell exhibits the higher peak current density, the larger peak area and the smaller value of Δ<i>E</i><sub>p</sub>, indicating that the NBTP-0.01//NMO one has the better electrode reaction activity, and the higher charge/discharge specific capacity. This further suggests that the NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> system doped with appropriate amounts of bismuth has the better electrochemical performance, which is consistent with the result obtained from the above-mentioned charge/discharge curves in Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0005">5</a> and <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0007">7</a> for the two half-cells.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="batt202400767-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/fbbdd87c-2676-49c6-a7b6-b538ff73ed5b/batt202400767-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/fbbdd87c-2676-49c6-a7b6-b538ff73ed5b/batt202400767-fig-0009-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/ab0daded-e44a-45d7-9056-5a0ce0f77374/batt202400767-fig-0009-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/fbbdd87c-2676-49c6-a7b6-b538ff73ed5b/batt202400767-fig-0009-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 9<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=batt202400767-fig-0009&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fbatt.202400767" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>cyclic voltammograms (CV) (a), charge/discharge plots (b, c), rate performance at different C-rates (d), and cyclic performances at 2 C-rate (e) and 10 C-rate (f) for the NTP//NMO and NBTP-0.01//NMO full cells.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>In this work, the charge/discharge capacities were estimated based on the mass of the active materials (NTP/C or Bi-doped NTP/C, with the theoretical capacity of about 133 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) of the anode. The charge/discharge plots at different C-rates for the NTP//NMO and NBTP-0.01//NMO full cells are shown in Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9b</a> and <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">c</a>, respectively. It can be observed that there are flat charge/discharge plateaus and high reversible charge/discharge capacities for the above-mentioned two full cells, as clearly observed from the plots in Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9b</a> and <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">c</a>. Moreover, it can be seen that the largest discharge voltage plateaus for the two cells are approximately 1.1 V (at 2 C-rate) in this work. Additionally, the corresponding overpotential of the NBTP-0.01//NMO full cell during the charge/discharge process is fairly smaller than that of the NTP//NMO one, suggesting that the Bi doping into NTP might decrease the polarization of the NTP/C anode during the electrochemical reaction process, thus enhancing the electrochemical reversibility of NTP during the charge/discharge process. The obtained results are in accord with those from the CV curves in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9a</a>. Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9d</a> presents the plots of discharge capacity vs. cycle number for the NTP//NMO and NBTP-0.01//NMO full cells at 2, 5, 10, 20 C and back to 2 C rates. The NBTP-0.01//NMO full cell delivers discharge specific capacities of 94.5, 82.7, 74.5, 55.8, and 92.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 2, 5, 10, 20 C, and back to 2 C rates, respectively, which are much larger than those of the NTP//NMO full cell (79.5, 73.9, 66.6, 54.0, and 77.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). It is indicated that the doping of the appropriate amount of bismuth into NTP can increase the discharge capacity of the full cell from 79.5 to 94.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> by about 18.9 %. Furthermore, the NBTP-0.01//NMO full cell reaps a large capacity retention of 97.8 % after the final 10 cycles at 2 C-rate, with that of 97.6 % for the NTP//NMO one, indicating the excellent inherent structural stability of the corresponding anodes. The obtained results are in accord with those from the charge/discharge curves for the NBTP-0.01 half-cells in Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0005">5b</a>~c.</p>
         
         <p>Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9e</a> shows the plots of specific capacity and coulombic efficiency as a function of cycle number for the above-mentioned full cells at 2 C-rate for 800 cycles. It can be observed that both the full cells have a very high coulombic efficiency of around 99 % during the charge/discharge processes. Additionally, the NBTP-0.01//NMO cell exhibits the better cycling performance with a larger capacity retention of about 80.1 % in contrast with the NTP//NMO one (71.2 %) after 800 cycles at 2 C-rate, as obtained from the plots of Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9e</a>. Furthermore, the plots of specific capacity and coulombic efficiency vs. cycle number at 10 C-rate for 1400 cycles were presented in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9f</a>. It also indicates that the above-mentioned two cells show a very high coulombic efficiency of around 99 %. Moreover, the NBTP-0.01//NMO cell also delivers a higher capacity retention of about 80.2 % than that of the NTP//NMO one (56.2 %) after 1400 cycles at 10 C-rate, as obtained from the plots of Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9f</a>. Based on the above results, it is concluded that that the bismuth doping into NTP can greatly improve the cycling performance of the corresponding full cell, as similarly reported in the plots of Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0007">7</a> for the corresponding half cells. Thereby, it is further confirmed that the introduction of bismuth ions slightly makes the cell size larger, and the possible solid BiO<sub>6</sub> serves as a stable and larger diffusion channel for the migration of Na<sup>+</sup> within the NTP structure, thus exhibiting a longer cycle life and higher rate performance for the modified composites in contrast with the pristine one. However, it should be noted that some small regular capacity fluctuations can be observed from the plots of specific capacity vs. cycle number in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9f</a>. Since both the NMO and NTP electrodes in the NTP//NMO full cell have excellent structural stability during high-rate electrochemical reactions in water,<span><sup><a href="#batt202400767-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202400767-bib-0053_R_d261297400e1963" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Adv. Energy Mater.">53</a></sup></span> it should be considered that the above-mentioned regular slight capacity fluctuations might be due to some unexpected changes in the environmental room temperature during the charge/discharge long-cycling processes.</p>
         
         <p>In addition, due to that the electrochemical reaction processes at the electrodes of the full cells, especially the oxygen evolution reaction at the cathode and the hydrogen evolution reaction at the anode during the charge processes, can be easily affected with the change of the charge voltage, Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0010">10a</a>–<a href="#batt202400767-fig-0010">c</a> also illustrate the charge/discharge curves with varying charge cut-off voltages such as 2.1, 2.2 and 2.3 V for the above-mentioned two full cells at a 1 C-rate. It can be also obtained that the NMO cathode can be fully charged before oxygen evolution occurs in this work, as observed from the CV curves in Figure <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0009">9a</a> when the NMO materials were used as the working electrode during the CV tests. Thus, it can be easy to understand that the hydrogen evolution reaction at the anode is more likely to occur in comparison with the oxygen evolution reaction at the cathode for the full cells during the charging processes, as also reported by Ref [42]. That is to say, the higher charge cut-off voltage of the full cell results in the more possible occurrence of the hydrogen evolution at the anode. It can be clearly seen that there is a new plateau in the NTP//NMO full-cell charge curve at 2.3 V, not at the lower charge cut-off voltages (2.1, 2.2 V), corresponding to the hydrogen evolution at the anode that occurs at the end of the charging process. Moreover, no new plateau in the NBTP-0.01//NMO full-cell charge curves can be observed at the end of the charging processes at the charge cut-off voltages including 2.1, 2.2 or 2.3 V. Thereby, there is more evident hydrogen evolution on the charging curves of the NTP//NMO full cell in contrast with that of the NBTP-0.01//NMO one, as observed in Figures <a href="#batt202400767-fig-0010">10a</a>–<a href="#batt202400767-fig-0010">c</a>. It suggests that the occurrence of hydrogen evolution for the NTP//NMO full-cell is indeed suppressed by the Bi doping into NTP. Furthermore, the inhibition of hydrogen evolution resulted from the Bi doping can decrease the irreversible depletion of the limited Na<sup>+</sup> in the cathode material and hinder the deterioration of the charge/discharge performance of the full cell, which is of great importance for the stability of the energy storage device. In addition, the Bi doping can suppress the hydrogen evolution reaction at the anode, thereby broadening the charge cut-off voltage of the full cell and enhancing the battery capacity. Then, the discharge specific capacity and energy density for the NTP//NMO full cell with the voltage range of 0–2.2 V is 80.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and 63.9 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Meanwhile, the corresponding values for the NBTP-0.01//NMO full cell with the voltage range of 0–2.3 V is 98.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and 75.0 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>. It should be also noted that the above-mentioned charge/discharge capacities and energy densities of the aqueous anode-limited full-cells were estimated based on the mass of active materials (NTP/C or Bi-doped NTP/C, with a high theoretical capacity of about 133 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) in the anode, in an attempt to precisely illustrate the effects of the introduction of Bi on the electrochemical and charge/discharge performances of the modified anodes. It is further indicated that the expansion of the charge cut-off voltage resulted from the inhibition of the hydrogen evolution reaction can increase the discharge capacity and energy density of the modified NBTP//NMO full cell by 21.8 % and 17.3 % in comparison with those of the NTP//NMO one, respectively.
</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="batt202400767-fig-0010"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3aa53766-95f5-4180-83bc-b898d00967d8/batt202400767-fig-0010-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/3aa53766-95f5-4180-83bc-b898d00967d8/batt202400767-fig-0010-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/224477be-82ce-4750-9214-6a254159e3cb/batt202400767-fig-0010-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3aa53766-95f5-4180-83bc-b898d00967d8/batt202400767-fig-0010-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 10<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=batt202400767-fig-0010&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fbatt.202400767" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                     <p>Charge/discharge curves for the NTP//NMO and NBTP-0.01//NMO full cells with varying charge/discharge voltage ranges:(a) 0–2.1 V; (b) 0–2.2 V; (c) 0–2.3 V.</p></div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         
         <p>Based on the above results, the successful Bi doping could contribute to the inhibition of hydrogen evolution via regulation the electrode potential for hydrogen evolution at the NTP anode, also accompanying with excellent electrochemical and charge/discharge properties. The introduction of bismuth ions slightly makes the cell size larger, while the possible formed solid BiO<sub>6</sub> serves as a stable and larger diffusion channel for the migration of Na<sup>+</sup> within the NTP structure. Consequently, the modified NBTP-0.01 composite has the highest cycle life and best rate performance in this work. Moreover, the expansion of the charge cut-off voltage resulted from the inhibition of the hydrogen evolution reaction by the Bi doping can greatly increase the discharge capacity and energy density of the modified full cell in contrast with those of the pristine one, respectively.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="batt202400767-sec-0007">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="batt202400767-sec-0007-title">3 Conclusions</h2>
         
         <p>A series of bismuth doped Na<sub>1+x</sub>Bi<sub>x</sub>Ti<sub>2−x</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C (x=0, 0.005, 0.01, 0.02) composites were successfully synthesized by a facile sol-gel method. An appropriate proportion of Bi doping has little effect on the crystal structure of NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>. The Bi doping can increase the lattice parameters and unit cell volume of NTP, thus contributing to the larger transport channel for Na<sup>+</sup> in the NTP crystal structure. The NBTP-0.01(x=0.01) anode shows the best electrochemical performance among all the samples, might due to the larger diffusion coefficient and the effective improvement of the intrinsic ion conduction property after the appropriate amount of bismuth doping into NTP. The NBTP-0.01 anode delivers the discharge capacities of 130.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1 C-rate and 104.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 2 C-rate, while The NTP anode has those of 106.5 (1 C) and 94.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (2 C). Moreover, the NBTP-0.01//NMO fuel cell exhibits the better cycling performance with a larger capacity retention of about 80.1 % in contrast with the NTP//NMO one (71.2 %) after 800 cycles at 2 C-rate. Additionally, the above-mentioned two full cells show a very high coulombic efficiency of around 99 %. Furthermore, the NBTP-0.01//NMO full cell also delivers a higher capacity retention of about 80.2 % than that of the NTP//NMO one (56.2 %) after 1400 cycles at 10 C-rate. The improvement of the cycling performance of the system in this work might result from the possible formed solid BiO<sub>6</sub> octahedra served as a stable and larger diffusion channel for the easier migration of Na<sup>+</sup> within the NTP structure. It was also found that bismuth doping into NTP can suppress the hydrogen evolution reaction at the anode, broaden the charge/discharge cut-off voltage, and thus enhance the battery capacity. For half-cell tests, when the discharge cut-off voltage is set at −1.2 V (vs. SCE), it can be observed that a new voltage plateau with respect to the possible hydrogen evolution reaction occurs at the end of the discharge curve of the NTP half-cell, however, not observed for the NBTP-0.01 one. It reflects that the hydrogen evolution reaction at the NTP anode is easier to occur than that at the NBTP-0.01 anode. Then, for full cell tests, it can be clearly seen that there is a new plateau in the charge curve of the NTP//NMO full-cell at 2.3 V, corresponding to the hydrogen evolution at the anode that occurs at the end of the charging process, however, not observed for the NBTP-0.01//NMO full-cell. It further suggests that the occurrence of hydrogen evolution for the NTP//NMO full-cell is indeed suppressed by the Bi doping into NTP. It is obvious that the inhibition of hydrogen evolution resulted from the Bi doping can decrease the irreversible depletion of the limited Na<sup>+</sup> in the cathode material and hinder the deterioration of the charge/discharge performance of the full cell, which is of great importance for the stability of the energy storage device. The discharge specific capacity and energy density for the NBTP-0.01//NMO full cell is 98.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and 75.0 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>, while the corresponding values for the NTP//NMO full cell is 80.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and 63.9 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Thereby, the expansion of the charge cut-off voltage resulted from the inhibition of the hydrogen evolution reaction after the Bi doping into NTP can finally increase the discharge capacity and energy density of the modified NBTP//NMO full cell by 21.8 % and 17.3 %, respectively. This work of great significance to develop practical NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C anode materials, promote the stability of ASIB performance, and accelerate the commercialization of ASIB.</p>
         </section>
